🧠 Q1(c): Interpretation (EXAM STYLE ANSWER)
👉 Largest gradient magnitude = -0.25 entries

So weights:

bottom-left

bottom-right

top-right

👉 These change most.

WHY?
Because:

They correspond to active ReLU outputs

AND receive strong gradients from FC layer

👉 Key idea:

Weights connected to high activation + high gradient flow change most.

🔥 Q3 (Important Concepts)
3a: Max Pooling
Y
=
max
⁡
(
A
)
=
3
Y=max(A)=3
👉 Only one position gets gradient

So:

Only pixel contributing to max gets gradient

Others = 0 gradient

👉 This explains sparse gradient flow

3c: Translation Invariance (KEY THEORY)
Max pooling:

👉 Picks max value only

So if image shifts slightly:

max value often SAME

output SAME

👉 That’s why CNNs become translation invariant

Structural explanation
The weight 
w
12
w 
12
​
  gets the largest gradient because:

It participates in multiple receptive fields due to weight sharing.

It is multiplied by relatively large input values, especially the value 
2
2 in the top-left patch.

Those patches correspond to active ReLU outputs, so gradient is allowed to flow back.

The upstream gradients at those locations are negative, so their contributions add up strongly in the same direction.

So structurally, 
w
12
w 
12
​
  receives the strongest learning signal because it is repeatedly used in positions where:

the activation survives ReLU, and

the input value aligned with that weight is large.

Answer for Q2(c)
The center pixel has a stronger effect because it belongs to multiple overlapping receptive fields. Due to weight sharing in CNNs, the same filter is applied at different spatial locations, so the center pixel contributes to several pre-activations at once. During backpropagation, gradient signals from all those paths add together. A corner pixel, in contrast, appears in only one receptive field, so it receives far fewer gradient contributions.

Q3(c) Interpretation: Why max pooling gives translation invariance
The question asks why shifting the input slightly left or right may not change the output 
Y
Y or the loss when max pooling is used. 


Main idea
Max pooling only keeps the largest activation.

So if the image shifts a little, the exact location of the strongest feature may move, but as long as the maximum value stays the same, the pooled output stays the same too.

For example, in Q3(a),

A
=
[
2
2
0
3
]
A=[ 
2
0
​
  
2
3
​
 ]
and

Y
=
max
⁡
(
A
)
=
3
Y=max(A)=3
If a slight shift changes the feature map to something like

A
′
=
[
2
3
0
2
]
A 
′
 =[ 
2
0
​
  
3
2
​
 ]
then the max is still:

max
⁡
(
A
′
)
=
3
max(A 
′
 )=3
So the output 
Y
Y does not change, and hence the loss may also remain unchanged.

That is why max pooling gives a kind of translation invariance: the network cares more about whether a strong feature exists than about its exact position.

Answer for Q3(c)
Max pooling provides translation invariance because it depends only on the largest activation in a region, not on the exact position of that activation. If the input image shifts slightly, the strongest feature may move from one spatial location to another, but as long as its activation value remains the maximum, the pooled output stays unchanged. Therefore, the final prediction and loss can remain the same even when the feature location changes slightly.

Q3(c)
Max pooling gives translation invariance because it preserves only the maximum activation. If a feature shifts slightly in space but still produces the same maximum value, the pooled output remains unchanged. Hence, small translations in the input may not affect the final prediction or loss.

got three .pt files

That usually means your PyTorch code saved model checkpoints.

A .pt file is commonly one of these:

full model

model weights only (state_dict)

tensor/checkpoint data

If you got three .pt files, they are probably from saving different models or best checkpoints during training, for example:

MNIST model

Colored-MNIST model

ResNet / transfer learning model

Common save patterns are like:

torch.save(model.state_dict(), "mnist_cnn.pt")
torch.save(model.state_dict(), "cmnist_cnn.pt")
torch.save(model.state_dict(), "resnet18_stl10.pt")
Or maybe:

best_model.pt
last_model.pt
checkpoint.pt
How to know what each file is
Look at the filenames first. They usually tell you.

If you want to inspect one, use:

import torch

obj = torch.load("your_file.pt", map_location="cpu")
print(type(obj))

if isinstance(obj, dict):
    print(obj.keys())
else:
    print(obj)
If it prints keys like:
dict_keys(['model_state_dict', 'optimizer_state_dict', 'epoch', 'loss'])
then it is a checkpoint.

If it prints many layer names like:

dict_keys(['conv1.weight', 'conv1.bias', 'fc.weight', 'fc.bias'])
then it is probably a state_dict.

Cell 4 — Flexible dataset loader
This handles common .pt formats:

tuple/list like (images, labels)

dict like {"images": ..., "labels": ...}

already-saved dataset objects

class PTDataset(Dataset):
    def __init__(self, pt_path):
        obj = torch.load(pt_path, map_location="cpu")
        self.images, self.labels = self._parse_obj(obj)

        # images -> float tensor
        if not torch.is_tensor(self.images):
            self.images = torch.tensor(self.images)
        if not torch.is_tensor(self.labels):
            self.labels = torch.tensor(self.labels)

        self.images = self.images.float()
        self.labels = self.labels.long()

        # Make sure images are in N,C,H,W format
        if self.images.ndim == 3:
            # N,H,W -> N,1,H,W
            self.images = self.images.unsqueeze(1)
        elif self.images.ndim == 4:
            # Could be N,H,W,C
            if self.images.shape[-1] in [1, 3] and self.images.shape[1] not in [1, 3]:
                self.images = self.images.permute(0, 3, 1, 2)

        # Normalize if data seems to be in [0,255]
        if self.images.max() > 1.0:
            self.images = self.images / 255.0

        # If grayscale accidentally, repeat to 3 channels for C-MNIST model
        if self.images.shape[1] == 1:
            self.images = self.images.repeat(1, 3, 1, 1)

        assert self.images.ndim == 4, f"Expected 4D images, got {self.images.shape}"
        assert self.images.shape[1] == 3, f"Expected 3 channels, got {self.images.shape}"
        assert len(self.images) == len(self.labels), "Images and labels length mismatch"

    def _parse_obj(self, obj):
        # Case 1: tuple/list -> (images, labels)
        if isinstance(obj, (tuple, list)) and len(obj) >= 2:
            return obj[0], obj[1]

        # Case 2: dict
        if isinstance(obj, dict):
            image_keys = ["images", "x", "data", "X"]
            label_keys = ["labels", "y", "targets", "Y"]

            img = None
            lbl = None

            for k in image_keys:
                if k in obj:
                    img = obj[k]
                    break

            for k in label_keys:
                if k in obj:
                    lbl = obj[k]
                    break

            if img is not None and lbl is not None:
                return img, lbl

            print("Available dict keys:", obj.keys())
            raise ValueError("Could not find image/label keys in dict.")

        # Case 3: dataset-like object
        if hasattr(obj, "__len__") and hasattr(obj, "__getitem__"):
            imgs, labs = [], []
            for i in range(len(obj)):
                item = obj[i]
                if isinstance(item, (tuple, list)) and len(item) >= 2:
                    imgs.append(item[0])
                    labs.append(item[1])
                else:
                    raise ValueError("Dataset items are not in (image, label) format.")
            return torch.stack([torch.as_tensor(x) for x in imgs]), torch.as_tensor(labs)

        raise ValueError(f"Unsupported .pt format: {type(obj)}")

    def __len__(self):
        return len(self.labels)

    def __getitem__(self, idx):
        return self.images[idx], self.labels[idx]

Cell 6 — Show sample images
def show_samples(dataset, n=8):
    plt.figure(figsize=(14, 3))
    for i in range(n):
        img, label = dataset[i]
        img = img.permute(1, 2, 0).numpy()
        plt.subplot(1, n, i + 1)
        plt.imshow(img)
        plt.title(f"y={label.item()}")
        plt.axis("off")
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.show()

show_samples(full_train_dataset, n=8)

train_size = len(full_train_dataset) - val_size

    full_train_dataset,
    [train_size, val_size],
    generator=torch.Generator().manual_seed(42)
)

Cell 8 — CNN model from scratch
This stays small and appropriate for the assignment.

class ColoredMNISTCNN(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, num_classes=10):
        super().__init__()

        self.features = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Conv2d(3, 16, kernel_size=3, padding=1),   # -> 16 x 28 x 28
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                              # -> 16 x 14 x 14

            nn.Conv2d(16, 32, kernel_size=3, padding=1), # -> 32 x 14 x 14
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                              # -> 32 x 7 x 7

            nn.Conv2d(32, 48, kernel_size=3, padding=1), # -> 48 x 7 x 7
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.AdaptiveAvgPool2d((4, 4))                 # -> 48 x 4 x 4
        )

        self.classifier = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Flatten(),
            nn.Linear(48 * 4 * 4, 64),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Dropout(0.2),
            nn.Linear(64, num_classes)
        )

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.features(x)
        x = self.classifier(x)
        return x

model = ColoredMNISTCNN().to(device)

num_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
print(model)
print("Trainable parameters:", num_params)
Cell 9 — Training and evaluation functions
criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
optimizer = optim.Adam(model.parameters(), lr=1e-3)

def evaluate(model, loader, criterion):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images = images.to(device)
            labels = labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    avg_loss = total_loss / total
    acc = correct / total
    return avg_loss, acc

def train_one_epoch(model, loader, criterion, optimizer):
    model.train()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images = images.to(device)
        labels = labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    avg_loss = total_loss / total
    acc = correct / total
    return avg_loss, acc
Cell 10 — Full training loop
num_epochs = 10

history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "val_loss": [],
    "val_acc": []
}

best_val_acc = 0.0
best_model_path = "best_colored_mnist_cnn.pt"

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch(model, train_loader, criterion, optimizer)
    val_loss, val_acc = evaluate(model, val_loader, criterion)

    history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    history["val_loss"].append(val_loss)
    history["val_acc"].append(val_acc)

    if val_acc > best_val_acc:
        best_val_acc = val_acc
        torch.save(model.state_dict(), best_model_path)

    print(
        f"Epoch [{epoch+1}/{num_epochs}] | "
        f"Train Loss: {train_loss:.4f} | Train Acc: {train_acc:.4f} | "
        f"Val Loss: {val_loss:.4f} | Val Acc: {val_acc:.4f}"
    )

print("Best val acc:", best_val_acc)
Cell 11 — Plot loss and accuracy curves
epochs = range(1, num_epochs + 1)

plt.figure(figsize=(7, 4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_loss"], label="Train Loss")
plt.plot(epochs, history["val_loss"], label="Val Loss")
plt.xlabel("Epoch")
plt.ylabel("Loss")
plt.title("Training vs Validation Loss")
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

plt.figure(figsize=(7, 4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_acc"], label="Train Accuracy")
plt.plot(epochs, history["val_acc"], label="Val Accuracy")
plt.xlabel("Epoch")
plt.ylabel("Accuracy")
plt.title("Training vs Validation Accuracy")
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()
Cell 12 — Load best model and evaluate on both test sets
best_model = ColoredMNISTCNN().to(device)
best_model.load_state_dict(torch.load(best_model_path, map_location=device))

test_biased_loss, test_biased_acc = evaluate(best_model, test_biased_loader, criterion)
test_unbiased_loss, test_unbiased_acc = evaluate(best_model, test_unbiased_loader, criterion)

print(f"Biased Test Loss: {test_biased_loss:.4f}")
print(f"Biased Test Accuracy: {test_biased_acc:.4f}")

print(f"Unbiased Test Loss: {test_unbiased_loss:.4f}")
print(f"Unbiased Test Accuracy: {test_unbiased_acc:.4f}")

Cell 14 — First-layer filter visualization for report
This helps for the “filters as images” style discussion.

def show_first_layer_filters(model):
    weights = model.features[0].weight.data.cpu()  # shape: [out_channels, 3, k, k]
    n_filters = min(16, weights.shape[0])

    plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
    for i in range(n_filters):
        w = weights[i]

        # Normalize each filter for display
        w_min, w_max = w.min(), w.max()
        w_img = (w - w_min) / (w_max - w_min + 1e-8)
        w_img = w_img.permute(1, 2, 0).numpy()

        plt.subplot(4, 4, i + 1)
        plt.imshow(w_img)
        plt.axis("off")
        plt.title(f"F{i+1}")
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.show()

show_first_layer_filters(best_model)

✅ Cell 5 — CNN Model (under 50k params)
class MNIST_CNN(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__()

        self.features = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Conv2d(1, 16, 3, padding=1),  # 16x28x28
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                 # 16x14x14

            nn.Conv2d(16, 32, 3, padding=1), # 32x14x14
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                 # 32x7x7
        )

        self.classifier = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Flatten(),
            nn.Linear(32 * 7 * 7, 64),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Linear(64, 10)
        )

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.features(x)
        x = self.classifier(x)
        return x

model = MNIST_CNN().to(device)

# Parameter count
num_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
print("Trainable parameters:", num_params)
👉 This stays under 50k parameters (assignment constraint)

✅ Cell 6 — Training setup
criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
optimizer = optim.Adam(model.parameters(), lr=1e-3)
✅ Cell 7 — Train & Evaluate functions
def train_one_epoch(model, loader):
    model.train()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0, 0, 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate(model, loader):
    model.eval()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0, 0, 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total
✅ Cell 8 — Training loop
num_epochs = 10

history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "val_loss": [],
    "val_acc": []
}

best_val_acc = 0

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch(model, train_loader)
    val_loss, val_acc = evaluate(model, val_loader)

    history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    history["val_loss"].append(val_loss)
    history["val_acc"].append(val_acc)

    print(f"Epoch {epoch+1}:")
    print(f"Train Loss: {train_loss:.4f}, Train Acc: {train_acc:.4f}")
    print(f"Val Loss: {val_loss:.4f}, Val Acc: {val_acc:.4f}\n")

class MNIST_CNN(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__()

        self.features = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Conv2d(1, 8, kernel_size=3, padding=1),   # 8 x 28 x 28
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                             # 8 x 14 x 14

            nn.Conv2d(8, 16, kernel_size=3, padding=1), # 16 x 14 x 14
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                             # 16 x 7 x 7
        )

        self.classifier = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Flatten(),
            nn.Linear(16 * 7 * 7, 32),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Linear(32, 10)
        )

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.features(x)
        x = self.classifier(x)
        return x

Cell 6 — training setup
criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()

Cell 7 — train/evaluate functions
def train_one_epoch(model, loader):
    model.train()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0, 0, 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate(model, loader):
    model.eval()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0, 0, 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total

The filters in the first convolutional layer appear to capture simple visual patterns such as edges, lines, and basic stroke structures. Some filters resemble vertical or horizontal edge detectors, while others capture diagonal or curved patterns. These filters respond to intensity changes in the input image, helping the network identify boundaries and shapes of digits.

This behavior is expected because the first layer of a convolutional neural network typically learns low-level features such as edges and textures. These features serve as building blocks for deeper layers, which combine them to recognize more complex structures like digit shapes.

Cell 2 — Seed and device
def set_seed(seed=42):
    random.seed(seed)
    np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed)
    torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)

set_seed(42)

for p in [TRAIN_PATH, TEST_BIASED_PATH, TEST_UNBIASED_PATH]:
    print(p, "exists ->", os.path.exists(p))
Cell 4 — Dataset loader for .pt files
class PTDataset(Dataset):
    def __init__(self, pt_path):
        obj = torch.load(pt_path, map_location="cpu")
        self.images, self.labels = self.parse_obj(obj)

        if not torch.is_tensor(self.images):
            self.images = torch.tensor(self.images)
        if not torch.is_tensor(self.labels):
            self.labels = torch.tensor(self.labels)

        self.images = self.images.float()
        self.labels = self.labels.long()

        # Shape handling
        if self.images.ndim == 3:
            # N,H,W -> N,1,H,W
            self.images = self.images.unsqueeze(1)
        elif self.images.ndim == 4:
            # N,H,W,C -> N,C,H,W
            if self.images.shape[-1] in [1, 3] and self.images.shape[1] not in [1, 3]:
                self.images = self.images.permute(0, 3, 1, 2)

        # Scale to [0,1] if needed
        if self.images.max() > 1.0:
            self.images = self.images / 255.0

        # Make sure 3-channel
        if self.images.shape[1] == 1:
            self.images = self.images.repeat(1, 3, 1, 1)

        assert self.images.ndim == 4, f"Bad image shape: {self.images.shape}"
        assert self.images.shape[1] == 3, f"Expected 3 channels, got {self.images.shape}"
        assert len(self.images) == len(self.labels), "Image-label mismatch"

    def parse_obj(self, obj):
        if isinstance(obj, (tuple, list)) and len(obj) >= 2:
            return obj[0], obj[1]

        if isinstance(obj, dict):
            image_keys = ["images", "x", "data", "X"]
            label_keys = ["labels", "y", "targets", "Y"]

            images = None
            labels = None

            for k in image_keys:
                if k in obj:
                    images = obj[k]
                    break

            for k in label_keys:
                if k in obj:
                    labels = obj[k]
                    break

            if images is not None and labels is not None:
                return images, labels

            print("Available keys:", obj.keys())
            raise ValueError("Could not find image/label keys.")

        if hasattr(obj, "__len__") and hasattr(obj, "__getitem__"):
            images, labels = [], []
            for i in range(len(obj)):
                x, y = obj[i]
                images.append(torch.as_tensor(x))
                labels.append(y)
            return torch.stack(images), torch.tensor(labels)

        raise ValueError(f"Unsupported object type: {type(obj)}")

    def __len__(self):
        return len(self.labels)

    def __getitem__(self, idx):
        return self.images[idx], self.labels[idx]

Cell 6 — Show some training samples
def show_samples(dataset, n=8):
    plt.figure(figsize=(14, 3))
    for i in range(n):
        img, label = dataset[i]
        img = img.permute(1, 2, 0).numpy()
        plt.subplot(1, n, i + 1)
        plt.imshow(img)
        plt.title(f"y={label.item()}")
        plt.axis("off")
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.show()

show_samples(full_train_dataset, n=8)
Cell 7 — Train/validation split
val_ratio = 0.1
val_size = int(len(full_train_dataset) * val_ratio)
train_size = len(full_train_dataset) - val_size

train_dataset, val_dataset = random_split(
    full_train_dataset,
    [train_size, val_size],
    generator=torch.Generator().manual_seed(42)
)

batch_size = 128

train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=True)
val_loader = DataLoader(val_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=False)
test_biased_loader = DataLoader(test_biased_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=False)
test_unbiased_loader = DataLoader(test_unbiased_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=False)

print("Train size:", len(train_dataset))
print("Val size:", len(val_dataset))
Cell 8 — CNN model
class ColoredMNISTCNN(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, num_classes=10):
        super().__init__()

        self.features = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Conv2d(3, 8, kernel_size=3, padding=1),    # 8 x 28 x 28
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                              # 8 x 14 x 14

            nn.Conv2d(8, 16, kernel_size=3, padding=1),   # 16 x 14 x 14
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.MaxPool2d(2),                              # 16 x 7 x 7
        )

        self.classifier = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Flatten(),
            nn.Linear(16 * 7 * 7, 32),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Dropout(0.2),
            nn.Linear(32, num_classes)
        )

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.features(x)
        x = self.classifier(x)
        return x

model = ColoredMNISTCNN().to(device)

num_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
print(model)
print("Trainable parameters:", num_params)
Cell 9 — Loss, optimizer, train/eval functions
criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
optimizer = optim.Adam(model.parameters(), lr=1e-3)

def train_one_epoch(model, loader, criterion, optimizer):
    model.train()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images = images.to(device)
        labels = labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate(model, loader, criterion):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images = images.to(device)
            labels = labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total
Cell 10 — Training loop
num_epochs = 10

history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "val_loss": [],
    "val_acc": []
}

best_val_acc = 0.0
best_model_path = "best_colored_mnist_cnn.pt"

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch(model, train_loader, criterion, optimizer)
    val_loss, val_acc = evaluate(model, val_loader, criterion)

    history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    history["val_loss"].append(val_loss)
    history["val_acc"].append(val_acc)

    if val_acc > best_val_acc:
        best_val_acc = val_acc
        torch.save(model.state_dict(), best_model_path)

    print(
        f"Epoch {epoch+1}: "
        f"Train Loss={train_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={train_acc:.4f}, "
        f"Val Loss={val_loss:.4f}, Val Acc={val_acc:.4f}"
    )

print("Best validation accuracy:", best_val_acc)

These results are exactly the pattern your assignment wants you to observe. Training on the biased Colored-MNIST data produced very high accuracy on the biased test set, but performance dropped a lot on the unbiased test set. This supports the shortcut-learning explanation in the assignment.

So the model performs extremely well when the test distribution matches the training bias, but much worse when that bias is removed.

Report answer for Analytical Question 1.3
You can write this:

The model achieved 98.81% accuracy on the biased test set but only 81.67% accuracy on the unbiased test set, showing a significant drop of 17.14 percentage points. This indicates that the model learned to exploit the color-label correlation present in the training data instead of relying only on the actual digit shape.

Conceptually, the optimizer prefers features that reduce the loss most quickly. Since color was strongly correlated with the class labels in the biased training set, it became an easier and more predictive shortcut than learning more complex shape-based features. Mathematically, gradient descent updates parameters in the direction that most rapidly reduces training loss, so the network places large weight on color cues when they are consistently informative during training. However, when evaluated on the unbiased test set, that spurious correlation no longer holds, so performance drops substantially.

Simpler version
The model performed very well on the biased test set (98.81%) but much worse on the unbiased test set (81.67%). This shows that the network learned the shortcut feature of color rather than fully learning the true digit shape. During training, color was an easier and more consistent signal for minimizing the loss, so the optimizer relied on it. When the color bias was removed in the unbiased test set, the model’s performance decreased significantly.

Report answer for Analytical Question 1.4
You can write this:

To force the network to focus on shape instead of color, several strategies can be used. First, one can apply grayscale conversion or color randomization so that color no longer remains a reliable predictor of the class. Second, stronger data augmentation can be used to vary colors independently of the digit label, breaking the spurious correlation. Third, the training set can be balanced so that each digit appears with many different colors, ensuring that shape is the only stable feature. Fourth, regularization or domain-invariant training methods can be used to discourage reliance on superficial features. Finally, one can explicitly train on both biased and unbiased environments so that only robust shape-based features generalize across distributions.

Compact version for Q1.4
Possible strategies include converting images to grayscale, randomizing colors during training, balancing the dataset so that color is not correlated with the label, and training across multiple environments with different color-label relationships. These approaches weaken the shortcut signal and encourage the network to learn robust digit shape features instead.

Nice summary paragraph for your report
In the Colored-MNIST experiment, the model achieved 98.81% accuracy on the biased test set but only 81.67% on the unbiased test set. This large performance gap shows that the CNN relied heavily on the spurious correlation between color and label present in the training data. While this shortcut worked well when the same bias appeared at test time, it failed to generalize when the color information was no longer predictive. This demonstrates how neural networks can learn shortcuts that minimize training loss without learning the true underlying concept.

Cell 2 — Imports
import random
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.optim as optim

import torchvision
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
from torchvision.datasets import STL10
from torchvision.models import resnet18, ResNet18_Weights

from torch.utils.data import DataLoader

from pytorch_grad_cam import GradCAM
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.model_targets import ClassifierOutputTarget
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.image import show_cam_on_image
Cell 3 — Seed and device
def set_seed(seed=42):
    random.seed(seed)
    np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed)
    torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)

set_seed(42)

device = torch.device("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")
print("Device:", device)
Cell 4 — Transforms and STL-10 loaders
STL10 supports train, test, unlabeled, and train+unlabeled splits. We will use train and test. 

weights = ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT
preprocess = weights.transforms()

train_transform = preprocess
test_transform = preprocess

train_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="train",
    download=True,
    transform=train_transform
)

test_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=test_transform
)

batch_size = 64

train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=True, num_workers=2)
test_loader = DataLoader(test_dataset, batch_size=batch_size, shuffle=False, num_workers=2)

print("Train size:", len(train_dataset))
print("Test size:", len(test_dataset))
print("Classes:", train_dataset.classes)
Cell 5 — Load pretrained ResNet-18 and freeze backbone
Torchvision’s resnet18 accepts pretrained weights through the weights argument, with ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT mapping to ImageNet-1K pretrained weights. 

model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)

# Freeze all existing parameters
for param in model.parameters():
    param.requires_grad = False

# Replace final fully connected layer for STL-10 (10 classes)
in_features = model.fc.in_features
model.fc = nn.Linear(in_features, 10)

# Only the new head should train
for param in model.fc.parameters():
    param.requires_grad = True

model = model.to(device)

trainable_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
total_params = sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters())

print(model)
print("Trainable params:", trainable_params)
print("Total params:", total_params)
Cell 6 — Loss, optimizer, train/eval functions
criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
optimizer = optim.Adam(model.fc.parameters(), lr=1e-3)

def train_one_epoch(model, loader, criterion, optimizer):
    model.train()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images = images.to(device)
        labels = labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total

def evaluate(model, loader, criterion):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images = images.to(device)
            labels = labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total
Cell 7 — Train the classification head
num_epochs = 10

history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "test_loss": [],
    "test_acc": []
}

best_test_acc = 0.0
best_model_path = "best_resnet18_stl10_head_only.pt"

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch(model, train_loader, criterion, optimizer)
    test_loss, test_acc = evaluate(model, test_loader, criterion)

    history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    history["test_loss"].append(test_loss)
    history["test_acc"].append(test_acc)

    if test_acc > best_test_acc:
        best_test_acc = test_acc
        torch.save(model.state_dict(), best_model_path)

    print(
        f"Epoch {epoch+1}: "
        f"Train Loss={train_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={train_acc:.4f}, "
        f"Test Loss={test_loss:.4f}, Test Acc={test_acc:.4f}"
    )

print("Best test accuracy:", best_test_acc)
Cell 8 — Plot curves
epochs = range(1, num_epochs + 1)

plt.figure(figsize=(7, 4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_loss"], label="Train Loss")
plt.plot(epochs, history["test_loss"], label="Test Loss")
plt.xlabel("Epoch")
plt.ylabel("Loss")
plt.title("ResNet-18 STL-10 Loss")
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

plt.figure(figsize=(7, 4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_acc"], label="Train Accuracy")
plt.plot(epochs, history["test_acc"], label="Test Accuracy")
plt.xlabel("Epoch")
plt.ylabel("Accuracy")
plt.title("ResNet-18 STL-10 Accuracy")
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()
Cell 9 — Load best model and final test accuracy
best_model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)
for param in best_model.parameters():
    param.requires_grad = False

best_model.fc = nn.Linear(best_model.fc.in_features, 10)
best_model.load_state_dict(torch.load(best_model_path, map_location=device))
best_model = best_model.to(device)

final_test_loss, final_test_acc = evaluate(best_model, test_loader, criterion)
print(f"Final Test Loss: {final_test_loss:.4f}")
print(f"Final Test Accuracy: {final_test_acc:.4f}")
Cell 10 — Get 2 correct and 2 incorrect predictions
For GradCAM on ResNet, using the last convolutional block is standard; for ResNet-18 that is commonly layer4[-1]. 

# A plain display transform for visualization only
display_transform = transforms.Compose([
    transforms.Resize((224, 224)),
    transforms.ToTensor()
])

# Reload test set without normalization for nice display
test_display_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=False,
    transform=display_transform
)

correct_samples = []
incorrect_samples = []

best_model.eval()
with torch.no_grad():
    for idx in range(len(test_dataset)):
        x, y = test_dataset[idx]
        x = x.unsqueeze(0).to(device)

        outputs = best_model(x)
        pred = outputs.argmax(dim=1).item()

        if pred == y and len(correct_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_dataset[idx]
            correct_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if pred != y and len(incorrect_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_dataset[idx]
            incorrect_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if len(correct_samples) == 2 and len(incorrect_samples) == 2:
            break

print("Correct samples found:", len(correct_samples))
print("Incorrect samples found:", len(incorrect_samples))
Cell 11 — GradCAM setup
The package provides GradCAM, and for image classification you can target a class with ClassifierOutputTarget. 

target_layers = [best_model.layer4[-1]]

cam = GradCAM(
    model=best_model,
    target_layers=target_layers
)
Cell 12 — Function to generate GradCAM overlay
# Same normalization used by pretrained ResNet weights
mean = np.array([0.485, 0.456, 0.406], dtype=np.float32)
std = np.array([0.229, 0.224, 0.225], dtype=np.float32)

def normalize_for_model(img_tensor):
    img = img_tensor.clone()
    for c in range(3):
        img[c] = (img[c] - mean[c]) / std[c]
    return img

def generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, target_class):
    # img_tensor is [3,224,224] in [0,1] for display
    input_tensor = normalize_for_model(img_tensor).unsqueeze(0).to(device)

    targets = [ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    grayscale_cam = cam(input_tensor=input_tensor, targets=targets)[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)

    visualization = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, visualization
Cell 13 — Show 2 correct and 2 incorrect GradCAM examples
all_samples = [
    ("Correct",) + sample for sample in correct_samples
] + [
    ("Incorrect",) + sample for sample in incorrect_samples
]

class_names = test_dataset.classes

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 12))

for i, (status, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label) in enumerate(all_samples):
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 1)
    plt.imshow(rgb_img)
    plt.title(f"{status} | True: {class_names[true_label]} | Pred: {class_names[pred_label]}")
    plt.axis("off")

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 2)
    plt.imshow(cam_img)
    plt.title(f"GradCAM Overlay ({status})")
    plt.axis("off")

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()
Cell 14 — Save the trained model
torch.save(best_model.state_dict(), "resnet18_stl10_finetuned_head.pt")
print("Saved model to resnet18_stl10_finetuned_head.pt")

📝 Task 1 Part B — Loss Curve Analysis (Use in Report)
Training Behavior
The loss curves show a consistent decrease in both training and validation loss across epochs:

Training loss decreases from ~0.51 → ~0.055

Validation loss decreases from ~0.14 → ~0.048

This indicates that the model is learning effectively from the biased training data.

Key Observation
Training loss is consistently higher than validation loss

Both curves decrease smoothly and stabilize after ~epoch 6

👉 This suggests:

no overfitting

stable convergence

strong fit to training distribution

Important Insight (VERY IMPORTANT for marks)
Even though the loss curves look perfect, the model still fails on unbiased data.

👉 Why?

Because:

both training and validation data come from the same biased distribution

validation does NOT test true generalization

model learns color shortcut, not shape

🧠 Core Concept (you must include this)
Loss curves alone are not enough to judge model quality.

👉 A model can:

have low loss

high validation accuracy

BUT still fail on real-world data

📝 Final Report Paragraph (strong answer)
The training and validation loss curves for Colored-MNIST show smooth and consistent convergence, with both losses decreasing steadily across epochs. The validation loss remains slightly lower than the training loss, indicating stable learning and no apparent overfitting. However, despite these favorable curves, the model performs significantly worse on the unbiased test set. This highlights that the validation set shares the same bias as the training data, allowing the model to rely on spurious color correlations. Therefore, the loss curves give a misleading impression of generalization, demonstrating that low validation loss does not necessarily imply robust performance across different data distributions.

🔥 Short version (if needed)
The loss curves show stable convergence with no overfitting. However, since both training and validation data are biased, the model learns color-based shortcuts. As a result, good loss curves do not translate to good performance on unbiased data.

how to include my handwritten notes on latex

You basically treat your handwritten work as an image and include it in LaTeX.

🧠 STEP 2 — Report Answers (WRITE THIS)
✅ Q2.1 — Why freezing early layers works
Answer:
Transfer learning works because early layers of a convolutional neural network learn general low-level features such as edges, textures, and simple patterns. These features are largely universal across different image datasets. By freezing these layers, we retain useful pretrained representations learned from large-scale datasets like ImageNet while reducing the number of parameters that need to be trained.

This helps in two ways: first, it prevents overfitting when the target dataset (STL-10) is relatively small, and second, it reduces computational cost and training time. The final layers are then fine-tuned to adapt these general features to the specific classification task.

✅ Q2.2 — GradCAM (correct predictions)
Answer:
For correctly classified images, the GradCAM visualizations show that the model focuses on the most relevant regions of the object. The highlighted areas typically correspond to distinctive parts of the object, such as the body or defining features. This indicates that the model is making decisions based on meaningful visual cues rather than irrelevant background information.

The concentration of activation on the object confirms that the learned features are aligned with human intuition, demonstrating that the model has successfully learned to identify important patterns for classification.

✅ Q2.3 — GradCAM (incorrect predictions)
Answer:
For incorrectly classified images, the GradCAM heatmaps often reveal that the model is focusing on irrelevant or misleading regions, such as the background or non-distinctive parts of the image. In some cases, the attention may be spread across the image instead of being concentrated on the object.

This suggests that the model fails to capture the correct discriminative features and instead relies on spurious or incomplete information. Such behavior can occur due to visual similarity between classes, insufficient training data, or ambiguity in the image. These errors highlight the limitations of the model and the importance of interpretability techniques like GradCAM.

✨ Optional (to get extra marks)
Add this line in Q2.3:

The misclassification may also result from domain mismatch between ImageNet pretraining and STL-10 images.

all_samples = [

You’re mixing two different tasks/models.

What the error means
Your current best_model is still the ColoredMNISTCNN:

it expects 3-channel 28×28 input

but you passed 1-channel 28×28 input from the wrong dataset path in that cell

That is why PyTorch says:

expected input ... to have 3 channels, but got 1
Also, for Task 2, best_model should be ResNet-18, not ColoredMNISTCNN.

Fix it properly
For Task 2, use a different variable name so it does not clash with Task 1.

Step 1 — rebuild the STL-10 ResNet model
Add a new cell:

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torchvision.models import resnet18, ResNet18_Weights

stl_model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)

for param in stl_model.parameters():
    param.requires_grad = False

stl_model.fc = nn.Linear(stl_model.fc.in_features, 10)
stl_model.load_state_dict(torch.load("best_resnet18_stl10_head_only.pt", map_location=device))
stl_model = stl_model.to(device)
stl_model.eval()

print("STL model loaded successfully")
Step 2 — make sure STL-10 datasets exist
Add this cell:

import torchvision.transforms as transforms
from torchvision.datasets import STL10
from torchvision.models import ResNet18_Weights

weights = ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT
preprocess = weights.transforms()

test_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=preprocess
)

display_transform = transforms.Compose([
    transforms.Resize((224, 224)),
    transforms.ToTensor()
])

test_display_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=display_transform
)

print("STL-10 test size:", len(test_dataset))
print("Classes:", test_dataset.classes)
Step 3 — recreate correct and incorrect samples
Use stl_model here, not best_model:

correct_samples = []
incorrect_samples = []

stl_model.eval()

with torch.no_grad():
    for idx in range(len(test_dataset)):
        x, y = test_dataset[idx]
        x = x.unsqueeze(0).to(device)

        outputs = stl_model(x)
        pred = outputs.argmax(dim=1).item()

        if pred == y and len(correct_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_dataset[idx]
            correct_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if pred != y and len(incorrect_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_dataset[idx]
            incorrect_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if len(correct_samples) == 2 and len(incorrect_samples) == 2:
            break

print("Correct samples:", len(correct_samples))
print("Incorrect samples:", len(incorrect_samples))
Step 4 — GradCAM setup
from pytorch_grad_cam import GradCAM
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.model_targets import ClassifierOutputTarget
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.image import show_cam_on_image
import numpy as np

target_layers = [stl_model.layer4[-1]]
cam = GradCAM(model=stl_model, target_layers=target_layers)

mean = np.array([0.485, 0.456, 0.406], dtype=np.float32)
std = np.array([0.229, 0.224, 0.225], dtype=np.float32)

def normalize_for_model(img_tensor):
    img = img_tensor.clone()
    for c in range(3):
        img[c] = (img[c] - mean[c]) / std[c]
    return img

def generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, target_class):
    input_tensor = normalize_for_model(img_tensor).unsqueeze(0).to(device)
    targets = [ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    grayscale_cam = cam(input_tensor=input_tensor, targets=targets)[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)

    visualization = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, visualization
Step 5 — show GradCAM images
all_samples = [
    ("Correct",) + sample for sample in correct_samples
] + [
    ("Incorrect",) + sample for sample in incorrect_samples
]

class_names = test_dataset.classes

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 12))

for i, (status, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label) in enumerate(all_samples):
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 1)
    plt.imshow(rgb_img)
    plt.title(f"{status} | True: {class_names[true_label]} | Pred: {class_names[pred_label]}")
    plt.axis("off")

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 2)
    plt.imshow(cam_img)
    plt.title(f"GradCAM Overlay ({status})")
    plt.axis("off")

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()
Why this happened
You reused names like:

best_model

test_dataset

from earlier tasks.

So the notebook kept the wrong model/dataset in memory.

Best practice now
For each task, use separate names:

mnist_model

cmnist_model

stl_model

and

mnist_test_dataset

cmnist_test_dataset

stl_test_dataset

That avoids these collisions.

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.optim as optim
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

import torchvision.transforms as transforms
from torchvision.datasets import STL10
from torchvision.models import resnet18, ResNet18_Weights
from torch.utils.data import DataLoader
Cell B — STL-10 datasets
weights = ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT
preprocess = weights.transforms()

stl_train_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="train",
    download=True,
    transform=preprocess
)

stl_test_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=preprocess
)

stl_display_transform = transforms.Compose([
    transforms.Resize((224, 224)),
    transforms.ToTensor()
])

stl_test_display_dataset = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=stl_display_transform
)

stl_train_loader = DataLoader(stl_train_dataset, batch_size=64, shuffle=True, num_workers=2)
stl_test_loader = DataLoader(stl_test_dataset, batch_size=64, shuffle=False, num_workers=2)

print("Train size:", len(stl_train_dataset))
print("Test size:", len(stl_test_dataset))
print("Classes:", stl_train_dataset.classes)
Cell C — Build ResNet-18 and freeze backbone
stl_model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)

for param in stl_model.parameters():
    param.requires_grad = False

stl_model.fc = nn.Linear(stl_model.fc.in_features, 10)
stl_model = stl_model.to(device)

print(stl_model)
trainable_params = sum(p.numel() for p in stl_model.parameters() if p.requires_grad)
print("Trainable params:", trainable_params)
Cell D — Loss and optimizer
stl_criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
stl_optimizer = optim.Adam(stl_model.fc.parameters(), lr=1e-3)
Cell E — Train/evaluate functions
def train_one_epoch_stl(model, loader, criterion, optimizer):
    model.train()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0.0, 0, 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate_stl(model, loader, criterion):
    model.eval()
    total_loss, correct, total = 0.0, 0, 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images, labels = images.to(device), labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total
Cell F — Training loop
num_epochs = 10

stl_history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "test_loss": [],
    "test_acc": []
}

best_test_acc = 0.0

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch_stl(stl_model, stl_train_loader, stl_criterion, stl_optimizer)
    test_loss, test_acc = evaluate_stl(stl_model, stl_test_loader, stl_criterion)

    stl_history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    stl_history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    stl_history["test_loss"].append(test_loss)
    stl_history["test_acc"].append(test_acc)

    if test_acc > best_test_acc:
        best_test_acc = test_acc
        torch.save(stl_model.state_dict(), "best_resnet18_stl10_head_only.pt")

    print(
        f"Epoch {epoch+1}: "
        f"Train Loss={train_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={train_acc:.4f}, "
        f"Test Loss={test_loss:.4f}, Test Acc={test_acc:.4f}"
    )

print("Best test accuracy:", best_test_acc)

def set_seed(seed=42):
    random.seed(seed)
    np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed)
    torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)

set_seed(42)

Cell 7 — train/evaluate functions

def train_one_epoch_stl(model, loader, criterion, optimizer):
    model.train()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    for images, labels in loader:
        images = images.to(device)
        labels = labels.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        outputs = model(images)
        loss = criterion(outputs, labels)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
        preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
        correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
        total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate_stl(model, loader, criterion):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for images, labels in loader:
            images = images.to(device)
            labels = labels.to(device)

            outputs = model(images)
            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)

            total_loss += loss.item() * labels.size(0)
            preds = outputs.argmax(dim=1)
            correct += (preds == labels).sum().item()
            total += labels.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total
Cell 8 — training loop

num_epochs = 10

stl_history = {
    "train_loss": [],
    "train_acc": [],
    "test_loss": [],
    "test_acc": []
}

best_test_acc = 0.0
best_model_path = "best_resnet18_stl10_head_only.pt"

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    train_loss, train_acc = train_one_epoch_stl(stl_model, stl_train_loader, stl_criterion, stl_optimizer)
    test_loss, test_acc = evaluate_stl(stl_model, stl_test_loader, stl_criterion)

    stl_history["train_loss"].append(train_loss)
    stl_history["train_acc"].append(train_acc)
    stl_history["test_loss"].append(test_loss)
    stl_history["test_acc"].append(test_acc)

    if test_acc > best_test_acc:
        best_test_acc = test_acc
        torch.save(stl_model.state_dict(), best_model_path)

    print(
        f"Epoch {epoch+1}: "
        f"Train Loss={train_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={train_acc:.4f}, "
        f"Test Loss={test_loss:.4f}, Test Acc={test_acc:.4f}"
    )

Cell 11 — collect 2 correct and 2 incorrect samples

correct_samples = []
incorrect_samples = []

with torch.no_grad():
    for idx in range(len(stl_test_dataset)):
        x, y = stl_test_dataset[idx]
        x = x.unsqueeze(0).to(device)

        outputs = stl_model(x)
        pred = outputs.argmax(dim=1).item()

        if pred == y and len(correct_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = stl_test_display_dataset[idx]
            correct_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if pred != y and len(incorrect_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = stl_test_display_dataset[idx]
            incorrect_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if len(correct_samples) == 2 and len(incorrect_samples) == 2:
            break

print("Correct samples:", len(correct_samples))
print("Incorrect samples:", len(incorrect_samples))
Cell 12 — GradCAM setup

target_layers = [stl_model.layer4[-1]]
cam = GradCAM(model=stl_model, target_layers=target_layers)

mean = np.array([0.485, 0.456, 0.406], dtype=np.float32)
std = np.array([0.229, 0.224, 0.225], dtype=np.float32)

def normalize_for_model(img_tensor):
    img = img_tensor.clone()
    for c in range(3):
        img[c] = (img[c] - mean[c]) / std[c]
    return img

def generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, target_class):
    input_tensor = normalize_for_model(img_tensor).unsqueeze(0).to(device)
    targets = [ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    grayscale_cam = cam(input_tensor=input_tensor, targets=targets)[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)

    visualization = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, visualization
Cell 13 — show GradCAM outputs

all_samples = [
    ("Correct",) + sample for sample in correct_samples
] + [
    ("Incorrect",) + sample for sample in incorrect_samples
]

class_names = stl_test_dataset.classes

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 12))

for i, (status, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label) in enumerate(all_samples):
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 1)
    plt.imshow(rgb_img)
    plt.title(f"{status} | True: {class_names[true_label]} | Pred: {class_names[pred_label]}")
    plt.axis("off")

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i + 2)
    plt.imshow(cam_img)
    plt.title(f"GradCAM Overlay ({status})")
    plt.axis("off")

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()
Cell 14 — save GradCAM images

os.makedirs("gradcam_outputs", exist_ok=True)

named_samples = [
    ("correct1",) + correct_samples[0],
    ("correct2",) + correct_samples[1],
    ("incorrect1",) + incorrect_samples[0],
    ("incorrect2",) + incorrect_samples[1],
]

for name, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label in named_samples:
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.imsave(f"gradcam_outputs/{name}_original.png", rgb_img)
    plt.imsave(f"gradcam_outputs/{name}_gradcam.png", cam_img)

    print(f"Saved {name}")

Cell 1
!pip install grad-cam
Cell 2
import os, random, numpy as np, matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import torch, torch.nn as nn, torch.optim as optim
import torchvision.transforms as transforms
from torchvision.datasets import STL10
from torchvision.models import resnet18, ResNet18_Weights
from torch.utils.data import DataLoader
from pytorch_grad_cam import GradCAM
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.model_targets import ClassifierOutputTarget
from pytorch_grad_cam.utils.image import show_cam_on_image

def set_seed(seed=42):
    random.seed(seed); np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)

set_seed(42)
device = torch.device("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")
print(device)
Cell 3
weights = ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT
preprocess = weights.transforms()

train_ds = STL10(root="./data", split="train", download=True, transform=preprocess)
test_ds  = STL10(root="./data", split="test",  download=True, transform=preprocess)

display_tf = transforms.Compose([
    transforms.Resize((224, 224)),
    transforms.ToTensor()
])
test_display_ds = STL10(root="./data", split="test", download=True, transform=display_tf)

train_loader = DataLoader(train_ds, batch_size=64, shuffle=True, num_workers=2)
test_loader  = DataLoader(test_ds,  batch_size=64, shuffle=False, num_workers=2)

print(len(train_ds), len(test_ds))
print(train_ds.classes)
Cell 4
model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)
for p in model.parameters():
    p.requires_grad = False
model.fc = nn.Linear(model.fc.in_features, 10)
model = model.to(device)

criterion = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
optimizer = optim.Adam(model.fc.parameters(), lr=1e-3)

print("Trainable params:", sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad))
Cell 5
def train_one_epoch(model, loader):
    model.train()
    total_loss = correct = total = 0
    for x, y in loader:
        x, y = x.to(device), y.to(device)
        optimizer.zero_grad()
        out = model(x)
        loss = criterion(out, y)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()
        total_loss += loss.item() * y.size(0)
        correct += (out.argmax(1) == y).sum().item()
        total += y.size(0)
    return total_loss / total, correct / total

def evaluate(model, loader):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = correct = total = 0
    with torch.no_grad():
        for x, y in loader:
            x, y = x.to(device), y.to(device)
            out = model(x)
            loss = criterion(out, y)
            total_loss += loss.item() * y.size(0)
            correct += (out.argmax(1) == y).sum().item()
            total += y.size(0)
    return total_loss / total, correct / total
Cell 6
num_epochs = 10
history = {"train_loss": [], "train_acc": [], "test_loss": [], "test_acc": []}
best_acc = 0
best_path = "best_resnet18_stl10.pt"

for epoch in range(num_epochs):
    tr_loss, tr_acc = train_one_epoch(model, train_loader)
    te_loss, te_acc = evaluate(model, test_loader)

    history["train_loss"].append(tr_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(tr_acc)
    history["test_loss"].append(te_loss)
    history["test_acc"].append(te_acc)

    if te_acc > best_acc:
        best_acc = te_acc
        torch.save(model.state_dict(), best_path)

    print(f"Epoch {epoch+1}: Train Loss={tr_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={tr_acc:.4f}, Test Loss={te_loss:.4f}, Test Acc={te_acc:.4f}")

print("Best test acc:", best_acc)
Cell 7
epochs = range(1, num_epochs + 1)

plt.figure(figsize=(7,4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_loss"], label="Train Loss")
plt.plot(epochs, history["test_loss"], label="Test Loss")
plt.legend(); plt.xlabel("Epoch"); plt.ylabel("Loss"); plt.title("STL10 Loss"); plt.grid(True)
plt.savefig("stl10_loss.png", dpi=300, bbox_inches="tight")
plt.show()

plt.figure(figsize=(7,4))
plt.plot(epochs, history["train_acc"], label="Train Acc")
plt.plot(epochs, history["test_acc"], label="Test Acc")
plt.legend(); plt.xlabel("Epoch"); plt.ylabel("Accuracy"); plt.title("STL10 Accuracy"); plt.grid(True)
plt.savefig("stl10_accuracy.png", dpi=300, bbox_inches="tight")
plt.show()
Cell 8
model = resnet18(weights=ResNet18_Weights.DEFAULT)
for p in model.parameters():
    p.requires_grad = False
model.fc = nn.Linear(model.fc.in_features, 10)
model.load_state_dict(torch.load(best_path, map_location=device))
model = model.to(device)
model.eval()

test_loss, test_acc = evaluate(model, test_loader)
print("Final Test Loss:", round(test_loss, 4))
print("Final Test Accuracy:", round(test_acc, 4))
Cell 9
correct_samples, incorrect_samples = [], []

with torch.no_grad():
    for idx in range(len(test_ds)):
        x, y = test_ds[idx]
        pred = model(x.unsqueeze(0).to(device)).argmax(1).item()

        if pred == y and len(correct_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_ds[idx]
            correct_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if pred != y and len(incorrect_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_ds[idx]
            incorrect_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if len(correct_samples) == 2 and len(incorrect_samples) == 2:
            break

print(len(correct_samples), len(incorrect_samples))
Cell 10
cam = GradCAM(model=model, target_layers=[model.layer4[-1]])

mean = np.array([0.485, 0.456, 0.406], dtype=np.float32)
std  = np.array([0.229, 0.224, 0.225], dtype=np.float32)

def generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, target_class):
    img = img_tensor.clone()
    for c in range(3):
        img[c] = (img[c] - mean[c]) / std[c]

    grayscale_cam = cam(
        input_tensor=img.unsqueeze(0).to(device),
        targets=[ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    )[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)
    cam_img = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, cam_img
Cell 11
samples = [("Correct",) + s for s in correct_samples] + [("Incorrect",) + s for s in incorrect_samples]
class_names = test_ds.classes

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 12))
for i, (status, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label) in enumerate(samples):
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i+1)
    plt.imshow(rgb_img)
    plt.title(f"{status} | True: {class_names[true_label]} | Pred: {class_names[pred_label]}")
    plt.axis("off")

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i+2)
    plt.imshow(cam_img)
    plt.title(f"GradCAM ({status})")
    plt.axis("off")

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()
Cell 12
os.makedirs("gradcam_outputs", exist_ok=True)

named_samples = [
    ("correct1",) + correct_samples[0],
    ("correct2",) + correct_samples[1],
    ("incorrect1",) + incorrect_samples[0],
    ("incorrect2",) + incorrect_samples[1],
]

for name, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label in named_samples:
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)
    plt.imsave(f"gradcam_outputs/{name}_original.png", rgb_img)
    plt.imsave(f"gradcam_outputs/{name}_gradcam.png", cam_img)

print("Saved GradCAM images")

Next step: define train/evaluate functions
def train_one_epoch(model, loader):
    model.train()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    for x, y in loader:
        x, y = x.to(device), y.to(device)

        optimizer.zero_grad()
        out = model(x)
        loss = criterion(out, y)
        loss.backward()
        optimizer.step()

        total_loss += loss.item() * y.size(0)
        correct += (out.argmax(1) == y).sum().item()
        total += y.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total


def evaluate(model, loader):
    model.eval()
    total_loss = 0.0
    correct = 0
    total = 0

    with torch.no_grad():
        for x, y in loader:
            x, y = x.to(device), y.to(device)

            out = model(x)
            loss = criterion(out, y)

            total_loss += loss.item() * y.size(0)
            correct += (out.argmax(1) == y).sum().item()
            total += y.size(0)

    return total_loss / total, correct / total

    te_loss, te_acc = evaluate(model, test_loader)

    history["train_loss"].append(tr_loss)
    history["train_acc"].append(tr_acc)
    history["test_loss"].append(te_loss)
    history["test_acc"].append(te_acc)

    if te_acc > best_acc:
        best_acc = te_acc
        torch.save(model.state_dict(), best_path)

    print(f"Epoch {epoch+1}: Train Loss={tr_loss:.4f}, Train Acc={tr_acc:.4f}, Test Loss={te_loss:.4f}, Test Acc={te_acc:.4f}")

print("Best test acc:", best_acc)

What this means for Q2.1
You can write this:

The fine-tuned ResNet-18 achieved a test accuracy of 94.24% on STL-10. This strong performance shows that transfer learning is effective even when only the final classification head is trained. Freezing the backbone preserves the useful low-level and mid-level visual features learned from ImageNet, while the new fully connected layer adapts those features to the 10 STL-10 classes. This approach reduces computational cost, speeds up training, and helps prevent overfitting on a relatively small dataset.

Also, your training behavior looks good
From epoch 1 to 5:

Train accuracy: 75.34% → 94.84%

Test accuracy: 91.37% → 94.24%

Test loss: 0.4093 → 0.1980

This suggests:

stable convergence

no serious overfitting

good transfer from pretrained features

])

test_display_ds = STL10(
    root="./data",
    split="test",
    download=True,
    transform=display_tf
)
Collect 2 correct and 2 incorrect samples
correct_samples, incorrect_samples = [], []

with torch.no_grad():
    for idx in range(len(test_ds)):
        x, y = test_ds[idx]
        pred = model(x.unsqueeze(0).to(device)).argmax(1).item()

        if pred == y and len(correct_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_ds[idx]
            correct_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if pred != y and len(incorrect_samples) < 2:
            raw_img, _ = test_display_ds[idx]
            incorrect_samples.append((idx, raw_img, y, pred))

        if len(correct_samples) == 2 and len(incorrect_samples) == 2:
            break

print(len(correct_samples), len(incorrect_samples))
GradCAM setup
cam = GradCAM(model=model, target_layers=[model.layer4[-1]])

mean = np.array([0.485, 0.456, 0.406], dtype=np.float32)
std  = np.array([0.229, 0.224, 0.225], dtype=np.float32)

def generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, target_class):
    img = img_tensor.clone()
    for c in range(3):
        img[c] = (img[c] - mean[c]) / std[c]

    grayscale_cam = cam(
        input_tensor=img.unsqueeze(0).to(device),
        targets=[ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    )[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)
    cam_img = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, cam_img
Show GradCAM outputs
samples = [("Correct",) + s for s in correct_samples] + [("Incorrect",) + s for s in incorrect_samples]
class_names = test_ds.classes

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 12))
for i, (status, idx, img_tensor, true_label, pred_label) in enumerate(samples):
    rgb_img, cam_img = generate_cam_overlay(img_tensor, pred_label)

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i+1)
    plt.imshow(rgb_img)
    plt.title(f"{status} | True: {class_names[true_label]} | Pred: {class_names[pred_label]}")
    plt.axis("off")

    plt.subplot(4, 2, 2*i+2)
    plt.imshow(cam_img)
    plt.title(f"GradCAM ({status})")
    plt.axis("off")

plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'shape'<Figure size 1200x1200 with 0 Axes>


Thought for 17s
This error happens because GradCAM needs gradients from the target conv layer, but your backbone was frozen, so the activations in layer4 did not keep gradient information.

Fix
Run this before creating cam:

for p in model.parameters():
    p.requires_grad = True

model.eval()
Then recreate GradCAM:

cam = GradCAM(model=model, target_layers=[model.layer4[-1]])
Keep your helper function like this

        input_tensor=img.unsqueeze(0).to(device),
        targets=[ClassifierOutputTarget(target_class)]
    )[0]

    rgb_img = img_tensor.permute(1, 2, 0).cpu().numpy()
    rgb_img = np.clip(rgb_img, 0, 1)
    cam_img = show_cam_on_image(rgb_img, grayscale_cam, use_rgb=True)
    return rgb_img, cam_img

Why this happened
During training, freezing the backbone was correct.
For GradCAM, you still need gradients through the conv layer, so turning gradients back on for visualization is the fix.

✅ Q2.2 — GradCAM Interpretation
You can write this directly:

Writing
GradCAM visualizations reveal that the model focuses on semantically meaningful regions when making predictions. For correctly classified images, the heatmaps highlight the primary object of interest. For example, in the horse image, the model concentrates on the body of the horse, while in the monkey image, the focus is on the animal’s face and upper body. This indicates that the model has learned relevant object-level features rather than relying on background cues.

In contrast, for incorrectly classified images, the model attends to misleading or non-discriminative regions. In the truck example misclassified as a car, the model focuses on the front portion and wheels, which resemble features common to cars. Similarly, in the airplane misclassified as a ship, the model places attention on the surrounding water and background structures rather than the airplane itself. This suggests that incorrect predictions arise when the model relies on partial or context-based features instead of the full object representation.

✅ Q2.3 — Failure Analysis
Writing
The model fails primarily when there is visual similarity between classes or when background context introduces ambiguity. In the truck versus car example, both classes share similar structural features such as wheels and front design, leading the model to confuse them. In the airplane versus ship case, the presence of water and dock-like structures causes the model to associate the scene with ships rather than focusing on the airplane.

These failures highlight two key limitations. First, the model sometimes relies on local features instead of global object structure. Second, it is influenced by contextual cues such as background elements. To improve performance, one could fine-tune more layers of the network instead of freezing the backbone, apply data augmentation to reduce reliance on background features, or use techniques like attention regularization to encourage focus on the primary object.

✅ Q2.1 (already based on your accuracy)
If you need it again:

Writing
The ResNet-18 model achieved a test accuracy of 94.24% on the STL-10 dataset using transfer learning with a frozen backbone and a trainable classification head. This demonstrates that pretrained convolutional features learned from ImageNet generalize effectively to new datasets. By freezing the backbone, the model retains useful low-level and mid-level features such as edges, textures, and shapes, while the final layer adapts these features to the specific classes in STL-10. This approach reduces training time, lowers computational cost, and mitigates overfitting on smaller datasets.

\section*{Overview}
This report presents the analytical and programming components of Assignment 3. The analytical section covers the forward and backward pass of the Toy-CNN, as well as the effects of pooling and normalization. The programming section includes (i) a custom CNN for MNIST and Colored-MNIST and (ii) transfer learning with ResNet-18 on STL-10 together with GradCAM-based interpretability.
